<Author>ValLandicho
<Content>Great Hotel Our family has been going to Waikiki since 1989 for the Honolulu Marathon either to run or see our running friends. In the last few years, we were staying in the Royal Hawaiian Hotel (Pink Hotel) but due to renovations from July 2008 to Dec. 2008, they were closed. So we decided to try out a similar hotel, Moana Surfrider.We booked 2 City View rooms in the historic Banyan wing during our stay, Dec. 13 to 22; one with the King bed and another with 2 double beds for our 18 and 19 year old kids. Relative to the kids' room, our room was smaller---there was plenty of space to walk around with a table for our laptop but we had a bathtub. The kids room was also on the 3rd floor and theirs had a bigger floorspace but they had an enclosed shower in their bathroom. Both rooms were facing Kalakaua Avenue (main drag on Waikiki)and although most shops are open until 11PM, the hum of the airconditioner seemed to drown the street noise below. If you are a light sleeper  like to go to bed before 11PM Hawaii time, I recommend you get an Ocean View room! Rooms have a small fridge, top-of-the-line really plush beds and 32 inch LCD tv with oceanic cable channels.The outdoor swimming pool has about 35 chairs  is relatively small but they have a part of the beach for Moana Surfrider guests roped off. You have to sign-up for any of these chairs by early afternoon the day before. This hotel has close to 900 rooms.There is gym on the second floor of the Tower Building with 5 treadmills, 1 stairmaster, 2 bikes, 2 elliptical trainers and a whole bunch of weight equipment. Each of the cardio equipment has its own TV monitor with all the Oceanic cable channels you can watch (just as good as Comcast back at home.)We ate at the Beachcomber (main restaurant) in the premises as we were celebrating my wife's birthday for dinner and although it was pricy, it was actually pretty good. Breakfast buffet was around $40 and dinner buffer was $80. Although this is a really nice hotel, we ate most of our meals outside: International Market Bazaar, L  L in Kuhio (plate lunches-mini $5 or $6, regular $7 to $9, Fattys (Chinese hole in the wall--2 items plus rice or chow mein for $5.50,) ABC stores for breakfast and snacks all over the place, Food Pantry (a couple of blocks away) for groceries or we take The Bus  go to Ala Moana Mall for shopping and their food court.The nice thing about the Moana Surfrider hotel is that it is centrally located for all the inexpensive food and the shopping and you're right there on the beach. Compared to the Sheraton, Pink Hotel or Outrigger on the Beach where you have to go towards the beach to get to the main entrance, the main entrance to Moana Surfrider is on Kalakaua!Most of the housekeeping is Filipino  since I am fluent in Tagalog, I talked to them everyday. Ever since Moana Surfrider became a Westin property, they have been pretty full compared to the other Westin  Sheraton properties in Waikiki.This is a very nice hotel  we'll probably be coming back next year. I highly recommend.

<Author>hoohiki
<Content>Good enough for Obama's press people and Hawaii Bowl festivities My husband and I returned to Waikiki to be reacquainted with the city and to introduce my 2 sons to the world famous landmark of Oahu. I chose to stay at the Moana Surfrider, a historical site, right in the heart of Waikiki so that we can take it all in. Our first impression was very positive. The valet and bellman were very prompt and courteous with their service. Upon registering at the front desk, we were met by a lei greeter and offered warm moist towelettes and cool wheatgrass with lemon grass iced tea. Nice. We were also upgraded from a city view room to a partial ocean view on the 15th floor, which made all the difference. I booked our reservation months in advance without knowing that the University of Hawaii football team will be staying at the same hotel before their game with Notre Dame in the Hawaii Bowl on Chrismas Eve. Not to mention, Obama's press people were also staying there and some reporters with the prime channels to telecast Obama's holiday retreat on the island. I was worried about the noise and traffic to say the least. But neither was a factor. In fact, we could barely hear a thing despite all the activities. I think it was a different story if you stayed in the older section with only 4 floors and facing the front. Our room was somewhat small, but big enough to fit 2 double beds. The decor was plain but the room was very clean including the bathroom.  The lobby and staircase was newly restored back to its original form in the early 1900's. Beautiful. The row of rocking chairs in the veranda, where guests can people watch is one of the hotels signature feature. The other feature is the afternoon tea in the courtyard under the old banyan tree planted in 1904, made famous by the old 1970's show, Hawaii Calls. My 2 boys greatly enjoyed this experience. I regret not taking the historical tour of the hotel and learning about its relation to the monarchs of old Hawaii. The hotel is amidst high end retail stores, but also scattered affordable ones. Restaurants, affordable and fine dining are all within walking distance. The hotel has a very small pool, but that's probably because the beach, with all its activity kiosks, is the backyard. My family had such a wonderful experience at the Moana Surfrider that we would highly recommend staying here to everyone.

<Author>Surfrat50
<Content>Great hotel in perfect location There are a number of reasons why this hotel is a great place to stay in Waikiki. I must say upfront, it was great to get the customary lei when we arrived late from the east coast. The staff was always very welcoming and accommodating throughout our stay.First, the Surfrider is quite unique in architectural design and to me, very upscale. True, there seemed to be lots of Japanese weddings, in the hotel but that could be true anywhere else in Waikiki. Second, the location is perfect. My son and I only walked a few yards to rent surfboards each morning. The surf break (Canoes) is great for kids and former surfers like myself as it's just a short distance offshore. The hotel's rooms were very nice - typical Westin. The view of the surf from our room in the tower was great. The courtyard featured an an ancient banyan tree that really set it apart from other chain hotels. Yes, the pool was a bit small, but when you have the beach at your doorstep who needs a pool anyway. Duke's restaurant is just next door. Outrigger and canoe rides were right on the beach nearby. The International Marketplace is just across the street. In terms of location, as a former resident of Honolulu, there is no better place to go for the full experience of Waikiki. Diamondhead is a short (2 mile) jog away. The zoo is just a couple of blocks away. Sure the rooms are a little pricey and you can certainly get cheaper places to stay, but all in all we really had a great time. The downside, if there is one...food in the hotel is high which is generally true anywhere you go. Also, the Duke's side of the hotel can be noisy late at night. Some guests have complained about other minor issues, but from my perspective, if you don't like the Moana Surfrider, I'm not sure what it takes to please you. Go there and enjoy yourself.

The same goes for the beach umbrellas and seats, we always found one but if you want to guarantee one you need to reserve the day prior. No charge for any of these services. The hotel bar had tasty drinks that ran about $5-6 for a beer and $10-12 for a fruity cocktail. We did not eat at the hotel for breakfast or dinner. There are a lot of options much closer for 1/3 to 1/2 the price. We did have a couple lunches and they were your typical bar type food. We did chuckle at the $80 steak for dinner. The restaurant was always full for dinner but the prices seemed excessive even by local standards.It was fun to see all the Japanese brides in the hotel. There were at least a couple each day. Beautiful. Every morning we ran a few miles around the area, you can get comfortable quick. We rented a car a couple days to go to the North Shore and check out the island but the hotel is close enough to so much, it wouldn't be necessary. I will post another review with tips for restaurants, car rental, transportation, activities, etc.

<Author>LAURIELLN
<Content>What a beauty ! We stayed (6) days at the Moana and (6) days at the Hilton Hawiian Village. We booked an Ocean View room w/ balcony in the Tower Wing, with a king size bed. Upon arrival, my husband and I were greeted with a lei greeting and a cold drink. The check-in staff was courteous, and greeted us with a smile. Check in was easy, and the hotel itself is the most beautiful in Waikiki.Location Location Location! Right in the middle of everything, no need to rent a car. Bus stop up the street if you feel comfortable taking the city bus. We opted to take the city bus everywhere. Cheap @ $2.00 pp.The pool is small, dont expect to get a lounge chair around the pool unless you make a reservation for one by 1pm the day before. I found no problem getting a beach chair and umbrella on the beach with no reservation at all. It was usually in the corner behind the lifeguard station, but I didnt mind. If you want a beach chair in the front row closest to the beach, then you HAVE to reserve one by 1pm the day before. Rentals for beach chairs and lounges around the pool are free, unlike the Hilton, which charges almost $60.00 for them!The beach area is VERY small and busy. And lots of waves if you like that sort of thing. the Hilton Hawiian Village had a bigger beach and calmer waters, but not close to the center of Waikiki, like the Moana was.The Moana closes their pool at like 5 or 6pm. The Hilton closes theirs at 10pm, and they have a spot-light on their beach, which allows for night swimming. Moana does not. Several people, including myself, went swimming until 9  10pm!Moana has an old-world charm that just takes you back to yesteryear. We spent several nights sitting on the front porch of the Maona on the rocking chairs watching the nightlife pass by-- Street-performers, street-hookers, and just regular patrons walking to the next shop.I noticed both the Moana and the Hilton have sensors on their sliding glass doors in the rooms that shut the air conditioing off as soon as they are opened. So, no air conditioning with the sliders opened, hence no listening to the waves crashing while your sleeping (unless you dont care about having the air on, that is).

<Author>MaisieNewYork
<Content>Can't Help Loving the Surfrider My boyfriend took me here as part of a two island birthday trip to Oahu and Maui (see Kapalua Villas separate review). We stayed in an ocean view room...although the bed was comfortable and the view spectacular, the room was a small and the bathroom very basic. The Moana's fitness center is actually situated at the Sheraton down the street. However, I knew going into it that the Surfrider isn't a five star hotel. That was part of the charm for me--the front porch overflows with older guests sitting on the rocking chairs watching the crowds go by, just-married Japanese couples resplendent in full wedding attire pop up in every corner of the hotel, the atmospheric Banyan Tree Courtyard buzzes with tourists savoring mai tais while watching the sun setting over the water and listening to the singers onstage...The service is what you'd expect at a solid four star hotel with a lot of traffic--very good and very friendly if a little distracted. But at the end of the day, the beauty of the Moana is in its history, architecture, perfect location on the beach, and walking proximity to most everything in Waikiki. I just loved staying there!

<Author>Nicole218
<Content>Overall Good Waikiki Choice We stayed at the Moana 8/1/08-8/8/08, the second week of our two week trip to Hawaii after coming from Maui where we stayed in a condo. We booked on the website in September and got a rate of $425/night for an Oceanfront room with Balcony, daily breakfast buffet for two, daily in room movie, and welcome basket on arrival. We arrived at 2:30 and were taken to check in desk while they took our bags up to the room. I was informed we were in a Diamond Wing Room, and I was kind of nervous after reading the reviews here. We were on the 4th floor. The room was NOT musty, and if anything my husband and I thought it smelled like brand new carpeting. The bathroom IS small and outdated, but we don't get hung up on that...If the shower is warm and we get clean towels that's all we need! We had an unobstructed view of the ocean and a balcony. These rooms are probably the best Ocean front as far as the view for this hotel. We were given two juices/macadamia nuts/chocolate covered pretzels/choclate covered macadamia candies/Macadamia Cookies, and Wasabi peas. These were great little snacks. It was nice having the daily movie included in the room as well. Breakfast buffet was nice to have include,d but I would be upset if I had to PAY $28/pp each morning. They always had a sort of sausage, scrambled eggs, poached eggs, bacon, has browns, assorted pastries/breads, fresh fruit, cold cereals/yogurt, and Japanese style breakfast as well. Included in the buffet price you can have waffles/pancakes/french toast/or omelettes made to order. Just seemed steeply priced for breakfast. We bought sodas/beer/alcohol/bottled water at ABC the first day and used the small dorm room style fridge in the hotel room. We took a collapsable cooler and took that down to the beach everyday with our water/snacks. As for the noise, there were daily wedding receptions on the Diamond Wing Lawn the week we were there, but all pretty much wrapped up around 11pm and didn't bother us. We were able to pick up WiFi internet access free in the lobby area with our laptop.We did not have a rental car until the last day to drive to the north shore- and we got this at the Budget at the Hyatt right across the street.I will agree with previous posters about the beach chair/lounge chair reservation system. It is absolutley ridiculous. While we were there, people would start lining up about 11:45-12ish though they don't take the resrevations until 1pm for the next day. It's just a silly way to do it. The chairs should be on a first come service in the am, and if LEFT unoccupied by 9am then staff could go and take towels off the chairs. We were so discouraged by this system that we NEVER used the pool or even the beach in front of the Moana. We walked ~50 yards to the Pink Palace and had nice lounging space everyday, as that hotel is closed now for the next year for renovations, and it is the widest stretch of the beach.Activities on Waikiki we did- WALKED to Diamond Head and then did the hike (took about 45 minutes to walk there, we did the hike in 20 minutes), Pearl Harbor (saw Arizona, USS Bowfin and Pacific Aviation Museum), took bus to Honolulu to see Iolani Palace/Aloha Tower/Shopping Center and Ala Moana Shopping Center (very nice!). Drove to North Shore to try to wade out to Goat Island (but was too choppy and rainy), then went up to Waimea Bay (lovely beach with fun jumping rock!) , saw Turtle Beach on the way back down and saw tons of turtles, even lounging on the beach (can see them from the road!). Overall, we most liked the service at the hotel and the location on Waikiki- we walked pretty much everywhere. Least liked the beach chair reservation system. The view was amazing, the bed was super comfy, and we would stay again if we go back to Waikiki.

The old lobby is stunning, and every staff member we met went above and beyond as far as friendliness and helpfulness is concerned. The sliver of beach owned by the hotel is pristine and beautiful, and the banyan tree in the courtyard boggles the mind with its size. During a three-day stay, my wife and I were quite content to remain on the hotel property almost the entire time, enjoying the beach and the ocean.

My complaint about housekeeping is this - we had to ask 3 times before an extra blanket and more towels were brought up. Not what I expect for a Westin property. The coffee place out front was a nice place to have breakfast - with the exception of a fellow tourist letting their kid steal all the milk set out for the coffee - not sure why the clerks let this happen. It's a lovely hotel. Rooms are OK size-wise, but nothing great. You have to deal with some noise, regardless of which class of room you get. Housekeeping was unresponsive. I'd recommend the other starwood properties over this one.

<Author>PMKF
<Content>Overall, disappointing We had one night in Oahu as a stopover from a week in Kauai, and chose the Moana Surfrider as a final slurge before heading home. The hotel is beautiful, with a lovely historic lobby, shady courtyard surrounding a huge banyon tree, and a nice, but small stretch of private beach. The location is excellent, although we weren't prepared for the traffic congestion (it took us almost an hour to drive 2 miles along Waikiki beach to the hotel) and the steep self-park/valet fees ($20 and $25, respectively). While the public spaces were nicely done, the room felt cramped. We requested an ocean front room, but ended up with a courtyard view in the historic Banyon wing, where you could see the ocean out of the tiny window if you craned your neck. However, since we were on the second floor, most of our view was actually the awning covering the dining room. Not the kind of view you'd expect for $350+ per night. The King bed was very comfortable, but we didn't get the restful sleep we hoped. The band in the courtyard played until late in the night. I finally had to turn on the TV and set the sleep timer to mask the load music. After getting to sleep late, we woke up early to muffled sounds of someone talking on a microphone - must have been in one of the meeting rooms near us on the second floor. I don't understand why someone would start a meeting at six a.m. on a Saturday morning, but that's apparently what happened. This appears to be a hotel popular for weddings and conventions. It was such a contrast to the peace and quiet we had on Kauai, where the only sound at night was crashing waves.

<Author>jlb3
<Content>Serviceable, tiny room We are Gold Preferred Guests and stayed in the hotel using points. So, to preface everything, when you get something for free, you can't really complain TOO much about it. If I had paid $400/night for the room we stayed in, it would have been completely unacceptable. The room was in the middle of the three wings of the now-combined resort, and it was TINY. It did have a somewhat-ocean view out of a small side window, but otherwise the room was dominated by the king-size bed. Beyond that, there was barely room to walk around. Compared to other Hawaii properties (i.e., the Hilton Hawaiian Village) which cost less, this room just did not cut it. However, it was clean and had a good bed. We also chose this property primarily because (a) it was free and (b) it was easy to drive from there to good beaches in O'ahu that aren't Waikiki. That said, otherwise this property was a solid Westin property. Staff were very courteous, including superior service at valet parking, which was our main concern. As I noted before, I used to live on O'ahu, and fortunately I already knew that Waikiki is the worst beach on this island and, as far as I know, throughout Hawaii. Although it has all of the tourist hotels, really, if you want a great experience on O'ahu, use Waikiki as your home base, and drive the 15-20min to other secluded beaches on the island. Since that was our plan, we mostly used the hotel for breakfast, where is a great buffet for $30 ($18 if you only eat cold food/continental). We also relaxed sometimes on the veranda in the middle of the property, where the pool and the excellent pool bar are. It is a beautiful area and one of the nicer layouts of the Waikiki properties. Compared to the Hilton, the Westin was also thankfully bereft of kids, which, since we don't have kids (it was our honeymoon) was important to us. The property is in excellent condition overall, and the fitness facility, while a bit tough to find (it's on the 32nd floor of the Sheraton tower, which is actually the 2nd floor, though not marked that way, and the signage is not great), was up to par and had all-new equipment. In sum, if I had a room with a balcony that was larger than a thimble, I would definitely stay in the Westin again. I would also stay there for free regardless. But, if I were paying their not-cheap rates, I would have been angry at the size of our room, but happy with everything else.

<Author>nctarheel06
<Content>Beautiful exterior and exceptional location We stayed here because my husband was attending a conference and I read the great reviews on Trip Advisor. Given that we were switching over from another hotel, I called the Moana Surfrider the morning of the switch and asked if early check-in was possible. As suggested by other Trip Advisor reviewers, I requested a room in the Banyan/Tower wing. They said there was room available and that I could stop by anytime. You are greeted with a lei and lemongrass tea at the front desk and they also gave a welcome kit to my 2 year old, equipped with outlet covers! I again requested a room in the Banyan Tower. The front desk person looked a little confused (apparently there's a Banyan Wing, Tower Wing, and Diamond Wing). I told him that I was advised to stay in one of the remodeled rooms. We were given a remodeled room next to the elevator in the Banyan Wing, which is also a historic wing, but most, if not all of the rooms in that wing, have been remodeled. The window opened out to Kalakaua Ave, which gave a great view of a few of the street performers at night. I should caution, however, that if you are a sensitive sleeper, you probably won't want a window facing Kalakaua Ave since you can hear sirens (the hotel is located next to a police substation) and music/loud noises coming from the street level.The rooms are somewhat small/crowded, but the closet is equipped with slippers, robe, and a safe and there is also a mini fridge under the flat screen TV. The TV was nice and so was the bed. There's also a cushioned bench runnning along the side of the wall with plenty of storage space underneath for your suitcases. The bathroom is nicely equipped with crevices for storage so even though the room feels small, there is ample space to store your belongings. The room, and the entire hotel for that matter, is very tastefully decorated. As onlookers pass the hotel, they can't help but to stop and stare at how beautiful the hotel is. Every morning within a span of 1/2 hour, you'd see at least 4-6 weddings pass through the lobby. The pool is on the small side, but I suppose it's adequate. It was nice having towel service for the pool and beach. I tried a $12 burger at the little poolside snack bar and it was surprisingly quite good.My only complains are pretty minor - beyond the first night, the housekeeping never replenished the toiletries. Couldn't quite figure that out but I just asked for extra toiletries when I passed a cart. Also, valet is $25/day and self-parking is $20/day. However, be prepared for a trek to get to you car if you choose self-parking. We ended up having to cross the street and walk through the Sheraton hotel to get to the elevator leading to the shared parking deck. It wasn't always easy to find parking either so I'd say that self-parking was definitely more of an inconvenience than we'd anticipated because the parking garage wasn't connected to the hotel. The hotel's overall location is excellent, however. Just a short, quick walk to countless restaurants and stores (both fast food and gourmet). Overall, a very enjoyable stay and worth the price that we paid.

<Author>Keskeret
<Content>Less than Perfect A week long February vacation in Hawaii, and the weather was perfect. The Westin Moana Surfrider however, turned out to be less than perfect.Upon first viewing, the hotel was spectacular. Who would not be wowed by it's colonial elegance, and the friendly check-in. We were accommodated however in the older 'historic' wing of the Hotel, and as soon as we exited from the elevator the mildew smell hit us. And then we opened the hotel room door and the heat emanating from the room was stifling.Okay, so perhaps a slight problem with the air-conditioning, and a bit of a mildew smell, but who wants to stay in their room when a fabulous beach beckons?The Waikiki beach was crowded, if it is long peaceful beach walks you crave, this is not the place for you. Nevertheless the water was clean and refreshing, and reasonably safe for small children. A word of warning though, the Westin commands it's own roped off area of the beach, with chairs and umbrellas. To guarantee one though (and shade is scarce), you must reserve the day before starting at 1pm. And if you want a chair in a better location, be prepared to tip. We didn't the first couple of days, and wondered why we were lodged behind the lifeguard stand with no view. The Hotel has maximized it's buildings to the amount of land available, thus there are no resort-style gardens for strolling and relaxation. The pool is small, and the Hotel fronts right onto a busy street. If you want a bit more of a lush atmosphere, then hotels further up the strip, like the Hilton, may be to your taste. Included in our room rate (as Platinum spg members) was a complimentary continental breakfast in their club lounge. A light selection of fresh fruit and miniature muffins. As Spg lounge breakfasts go it was on the lean side, with no daily variation. It was great though having the complimentary internet access. The Hotel boasts one main restaurant, the Beach bar, and a pool snack bar. The informal beach bar however serves it's food on plastic plates, even when you are not ordering from the beach area. The food was not very good. I cannot understand how the Hotel's food and beverage department, overseen by the same executive chef, can serve one star food anywhere, in a five star hotel. Do yourself a favour, and if you want to dine outside by a pool and watch the sunset, or soak up a few rays at lunch, walk up the beach and eat at the Outrigger, or Dukes, or the Royal Hawaiian, or the Sheraton, or the Hilton Hawaiian Village. The food is much better, and served on real plates. And splurge for a treat at Bali by The Sea at the Hilton. An excellent meal with great service!The Westin has a great location, right in the heart of the shopping district. The Hotel has a tour and travel desk and we booked several excursions. The Pearl Harbour tour was excellent and informative. The Polynesian Cultural Centre was okay. If you have never travelled to any of the islands covered (Fiji, Samoa, New Zealand etc), then you would find it interesting. Very expensive though. we took the city bus to Diamond Head and walked up to the crater. If you are not fit, or not wearing proper shoes, give it a miss. There are alot of steps, and we saw alot of people dropping out half way through. In all, the Westin Moana Surfrider, despite the charm of it's facade, the accommodation experience very much depends on the room you receive. If you are lodged in the old wing, be prepared for low-functioning air conditioning, the whiff of mildew, and small rooms that although clean, can still house cracked tiles in cramped bathrooms. The experience will be different should you receive a newer room. And in a top notch property, commanding high room rates for all rooms, that should not be the case.  
<Date>Mar 11, 2008

<Author>Fishstickman
<Content>Nice place, despite being in Waikiki My wife and I stayed at the Moana Surfrider in early Feb 2008 for 4 nights. I was in Honolulu for business and a couple days of vacation and my wife was able to come with me on this trip. We booked a cheap room directly from a special on the Westin website ($209/night). We got a city view room in the old section and were honestly just fine with that. The noise from the street in front of the hotel was noticeable, but the loud air conditioner drown out most of the noise. I'm not sure that an ocean view room would have been any quieter since they overlook the courtyard by the bar and they have live music every night until around 10 PM. For the rate, it was a fine room. Great bed, nice TV, rather small, but still fine. We asked for a late checkout due to an evening plane home and they accommodated us in an even smaller room on the same floor for $50 (that extended our stay until 5 PM).The staff was very helpful and nice. The Banyan bar is a great place, but everyone else on the Island seems to know it and it was swamped with people. If you could get the attention of a waitperson, you were in business, but it could definitely be difficult. Excellent Mai Tais and they have a good tequila selection at the bar. The food is bar food and mediocre at best. We shopped at the Moonbow store for clothes and the folks there were really nice and helpful.We self-parked across the street at the Sheraton and that worked out just fine (self parking is $20/night and valet is $25/night).We didn't eat at the restaurant, so I don't have any input. There is a good coffee shop attached to the hotel - Honolulu Coffee Co.Decent beach, smallish pool - but both fine.I'd definitely stay here again, but would try to go when the city isn't so busy. There were too many people in town for our taste and the hotel was as busy as the city. This is a beautiful property and has a LOT more character than most of the everyday chain properties have. It's a little more expensive, but is in a great location and is really beautiful.If you're going to Honolulu for the first time, I would recommend doing your research about where to eat, off of the Waikiki strip. Everything on the strip is very expensive and mediocre at best. We had an EXCELLENT meal at the new Roy's on Lewers St. Best poke I've ever had. We had an excellent time snorkeling at Hanauma Bay (about a 20-30 min drive from the hotel). Get there before 7 am and it's free and you'll have a better shot at seeing turtles - incredible. If you plan to go before 7 am, rent your snorkel gear before you go - the rental place at the park doesn't open until 7:30 or so.

<Author>vtextc
<Content>A charming piece of history with modern amenities and great service My wife and I just returned from our third trip to Oahu in as many years. This was our first stay at the Surfrider and enjoyed the experience so much that a review was in order.We arrived very late at night and weren't greeted by the customary lei and cold juice spoken about by other reviewers. To our dismay, our booking called for two twin beds; highly unsuitable for a couple celebrating an anniversary. The staff at the counter were overly accomodating in finding us a room with a king size bed, albeit in the Historic Banyan wing.The room was recently renovated (2007) with modern fixtures and furnishings, however was extremely small in size at less than 200 sq/ft. The shower cublicle was small, and the room faced onto the street with some traffic noise given poor insulation and older windows in this, the original 1901-era side of the building. I expected nothing more given the period of the room which was still very elegant and stately in nature. We ordered room service given our late hour of arrival, and the food was delivered promptly, albeit with a delivery charge of $5.00, and a 17% gratuity to boot. Generally speaking, we found the restaurants at the Surfrider a little dear, and the quality of the food was on par with other, better priced restaurants.The next morning, we inquired if a larger room was available, and indeed, staff were once again, very accomodating. We were given the choice of two other rooms which we were allowed to preview before selecting one. We settled on a large tower room, which had been renovated in 2006 but was significantly larger than that in the historic wing. The room was equipped with all modern amentities including a bar fridge and courtesy safe, however the cost of $4.25 for a litre of water seemed a little outrageous considering that the same bottle cost 99c at the ABC store across the street. That said, the room boasted a partial ocean view, despite being labeled by staff as a city-view room. We were overly pleased with the sumptuous bedding, and luxurious robes and slippers provided.The roped off beach area for guests was a nice touch as well, and despite being small and sometimes crowded, availability of deck chairs and courtesy towels was never an issue. Beachside service is quick and friendly, with staff delivering drinks/snacks directly to your location on the beach. I would advise/request that guests do not feed the numerous pigeons and doves that frequent the area since they do become quite boisterous at times and the mess they leave behind leaves little to be desired. The Catamaran services which pull up to shore directly outside the hotel are excellent value for money at $25.00 per guest including an open bar. Keep in mind that they are owner operated, and in no way affiliated to the Westin group. We rented a vehicle for four days of our stay and found that much like anywhere else in Waikiki, parking is at a premium. Valet parking costs $25.00 per day, plus the obligatory $5.00 or so in a gratuity, whereas you can park your own vehicle across the street at the Princess Kauilani for a reasonable $15.00.Our return flight home was a red-eye flight and did not depart until 2359 hours. The Surfrider staff were pleased to store our baggage for us after checkout which is at 1200 noon, as compared to 1100 hours at most hotels. The extra hour was a nice touch. In addition, the Surfrider provides a hospitality room for guests to shower and freshen up before their departure. Despite the room being available for only 45 minutes, staff were happy to deliver our luggage up to the room so that we could prepare for our journey.In all, we had a pleasant stay at the Surfrider and would stay at, or recommend the property to friends and family. In summation, here are a few highs and lows of our trip:Highs:-Historic significance of property-Accomodating/Friendly staff-Poolside/beach food and beverage service-Courtesy hospitality room for guests-Close location to other amenities such as catamaran ridesLows:-Exhorbant pricing of food and parking-Smaller rooms in historic wing (despite their charming appearance)-Noise (not unbearable) on city-view side of property

I realize we could have fussed unitl we were moved but we were in Hawaii so how bad could it be?? :)Like I said, the hotel was beautiful. The staff was friendly. Great location. If your looking for a buffet breakfast, go next door to Dukes. The food is good and the atmosphere was great. Give the Moana Surfrider a try. It truly is worth it. We actually liked it better than our next hotel- Grand Wailea. I can't wait to go back.

<Author>Chilipadi_can1350
<Content>Elegant, lively hotel! Great! From the outside, the Moana Surfrider is an elegant hotel, with a distinct, historic yet pleasing exterior. Upon entrance to the lobby and check-in desk, you will notice the openness of the lobby, with large (no doors) entrances into the hotel and out onto the patio/veranda and beach. Upon check-in, we are greeted not only by the usual room keys and hotel information, but, at the same time, a welcoming lei, towel to clean your hands, and fresh, cold juice. This may be slightly overwhelming, especially for travellers who are easily stressed and/or need to focus on checking in.After being handed our room keys, we go up to our room, and our bags are delivered promptly. The room is clean and well designed, and the beds are one of the best in the hotel industry. Unlike other hotel beds, with dozens of different layers, some dirty and some clean, you will feel right at home with these simple yet luxurious duvets. The bathroom has ample room.Looking at the TV, it seems travelers can't go to any hotel these days and watch normal TV: The technology installed on the televisions is slow and so cumbersome that it is likely that you will accidentally press the wrong button and buy one of their expensive movies. Even technically advanced people will have some trouble finding out how to simply watch the news! However, one benefit of this system is that it allows you to check-out via the TV, requiring no stop or delay at the check-out desk upon leaving the hotel, unless you need a receipt/copy of your bill (you will also automatically get a copy at the address of your credit card, a.k.a your home).Walking around the hotel, the veranda/patio is a nice, open-air area to enjoy some tropical drinks (try a tropical itch: it comes with a back scratcher!) However, beware of pigeons! As they inhabit the tree that overhangs the veranda, they frequently shed stool on hotel guests and anyone else who lounges under that tree!Have you gone through a lot of clothes? Dirty clothes? Long trip? The laundary room is close by. Enter the hotel through the main entrance, turn left and go down the hall until you reach the first elevator on the left. Go down that elevator to the basement, and go slightly right then forward. There you will find two top loading washers and dryers that cost $2 each. Soap is available. These are self-service coin machines, so you must pay in quarters. A bill to coin machine is in that same room.Furthermore, continental breakfast at the hotel includes not only the usual food, but, due to the large number of Japanese tourists, rice, japanese assorted food to go on top of the rice (seaweed, etc.) and miso soup! They also have a full, hot breakfast buffet, along with various menus to order individually from.The only complaint, a small one, as reported by one of my traveling companions, is that live music plays until 10:30 at night, which may disturb some people's sleep. However, this was only noticed from room 680 and those in that same section of the hotel.In conclusion, this is a great hotel, and I would strongly reccomend this to all other travellers. Centrally located at the heart of Waikiki, this hotel is clean, with lots to do and eat nearby!

<Author>konabound08
<Content>loved every minute! just returned from our christmas trip to hawaii, which capped off with a three night stay at the moana on 12/24, 12/25 and 12/26. i'd made my first visit there almost 30 years ago and had been eager to return. our visit exceeded my expectations and my husband and i can't wait to go back! the lei greeting, warm towels and lemongrass green tea offered at check-in was charming and made us feel like VIP's. we booked a city view room in the diamond wing so i expected a small-ish, older room. instead, we were upgraded to an ocean view room in the tower wing (#877). our room was spacious (even the bathroom!) and offered a large balcony. we were right off the elevator and, although my husband and i are both light sleepers, it was never a problem. the hotel looked fabulous for the holiday! there were signs acknowledging ongoing reno, but we never heard a thing. we especially loved: the location! <Author>mharnish
<Content>Alohah at the Moana I was first informed of the Moana by a local who had relocated to California and told me that is where she choose to spend her leisure time when she visits the island. The outside of the Moana Surfrider hotel is stunning, think classic old Hollywood charm. Sophisticated, glamorous and elegant is what comes to mind all while being understated at the same time.Upon arrival you're first greeted by the doorman who offers to help you with your bags in a very non-aggressive manor. Even before entering the lobby I spied rocking chairs that line the front and back porches of the property. The guests look at peace resting comfortably in the chairs some reading, others chatting and still more resting their eyes dozing in and out of what appears to be only pleasant filled dreams. Once inside we were escorted to the reception where we were immediately attended to and greeted with fresh flower leis and cool Hibiscus tea. Next a hot towel was handed to us by the staff who dawned traditional Muumuus and brought life to the Aloha spirit. This felt like an indulgence since our faces had dried after being in an airline cabin for the previous 5 hours.The lobby was just finishing a massive renovation so everything looked it's very best. I particularly liked the color scheme which was green with dark wood accents and white bright trim. It felt cool, crisp and relaxing to say the least.The rooms were equally as nice and welcoming with all the modern amenities. There was even a vacant mini fridge to store drinks and any left overs you might bring back. Strange in a time when most hotels have the fridge stock piled full so that they can bill you the second one of those electronic senors detects that you have removed an item. But the room is not the place you want to spend your time. Outside the ocean beckons you. Since check-in was at 4PM we we had just enough time to settle in by the pool and have our first Mai Tai before sunset was about to start. In the background a band strumming mellow Hawaiian melodies plays to the dramatic effects taking place in the sky.For never having been here before, I felt strangely at home in no time. It was back up to the room for a luxurious shower and then out the front door to discover what culinary treats await us. You don't have to travel far to find great eats and so we didn't . You could in fact spend your entire trip in and around this hotel and you would have accomplished nothing - exactly what is needed sometimes.If you get a chance, I'd recommend getting fresh seafood at Duke's next door - the omma was a great flaky, buttery fish that I'd certainly go back for. Across the street is Cheeseburger in Paradise which if you haven't been before is a must anytime you're on the island.Rental car service can be arranged through the concierge and picked up next door at the Hyatt - how convenient. Day trips to the North Shore offer a great change of pace. Of course, if you've never tried surfing before there are world class surf instructors on the beach in front of the hotel.Extreme value for the money and worth every penny. Do consider paying the extra few bucks to stay here as opposed to staying in another hotel that is located several blocks back from the beach. You will enjoy every moment!

<Author>thebutlerdidit
<Content>Terrific stay - we'll be back at the Moana Surfrider! After a couple of visits to the Halekulani on Waikiki, I didn't think my wife would ever want to stay anywhere else. It is a beautiful, classy, but expensive hotel. When I booked a Thanksgiving week trip this year at the Moana Surfrider (to save some money) I expected my wife would be disappointed. But she loved it. We stayed in a partial ocean view room on the 11th floor of the Tower Wing. The only ocean view in our room was out on the balcony, but we were glad to have that balcony (next time we'll pop for a full ocean view!). The hotel is being renovated and the Tower wing is finished. The furnishings, decorations and bedding are beautifully done. The room was spotlessly clean. The bathroom and the closet were a little small for us, but both of us brought too many clothes for oursix night stay and somehow we fit it all in. Although the rooms are about a third smaller than at the Halekulani, we didn't really feel cramped. The room was totally quiet - we slept great. We'd recommend a room on a high floor in the Tower wing. Westin thoughtfully put real refrigerators in the rooms, instead of those ridiculous mini-bars. The Banyan Courtyard is beautiful, the pool a little small but very refreshing, and access to the beach - including a private area with lounge chairs and umbrellas - is great. Waikiki is crowded - especially during Thanksgiving week - but we always managed to find room lay out between the pool and the beach and enjoy the weather, which was perfect (low humidity - we like November in Hawaii!). Whilethere is a snack bar and table service in the Banyan Courtyard, the Surfrider's signature restaurant hadn't yet reopened following renovation. (By the time you read this, it'll probably be open.) The best nearby dining options for dinner were right next door at the Outrigger Hotel - Chuck's Steak House, the Hula Grill and Duke's. We had Thanksgiving dinner at Roy's on Waikiki Walk - terrific.Our package purchased through Costco included the daily breakfast buffet, which we thought was terrific. I thought the Beachside Cafe where the buffet was served looked a little tired, but in the cafe's outside seating, the view of Waikiki is unbeatable. Ask to sit outside!After experiencing the Moana Surfrider my wife has decided that the Halekulani, as great as it is, is a little stuffy by comparison. (We did, however, have a beautiful evening at the Halekulani's House Without A Key during our trip.) And my wife loves the fact that the Surfrider is right across the street from her favorite shopping at Waikiki. We thought the service and the quality of the hotel staff at the Surfrider was first rate. And we were there during a peak holiday week when the hotel was full.I appreciate the fact that there are great deals to be had on this hotel, both through Starwood and through outfits like Costco and AARP.The Halekulani hardly ever has deals on its rooms. We did take advantage of an American Express 3-nights-for-the-price-of-2 deal at the Halekulani a few years ago. We haven't seen anything like it on the Halekulani since.I decided I would write this review before I see the credit card billsfrom my wife's Waikiki shopping sprees with her mother. If I have any money left, we'll be planning a 20th wedding anniversary trip back to the Surfrider next year for sure! If the hotel's upcoming new restaurant and spa live up to the rest of the property, I'll give 'em five stars next time.

<Author>rachlikesrhythm
<Content>The First Lady of Waikiki gets a makeover We stayed at the Moana Surfrider from Friday 13th to Thursday 19th July 2007.Our first impressions of the hotel were superb. It is a stunning building, particularly when compared to the concrete tower blocks scarring the Waikiki skyline.We were upgraded to an ocean front room and given a $75 food credit as we were honeymooners and were greeted with fresh flower lei's (pronounced lays - that confused me too!) on arrival. The hotel is currently under refurbishment although not a lot seems to be being done. The main foyer and reception area is completed and is gorgeous, but work is currently being carried out on the Banyan Wing (the middle historic part of the hotel) so this section was closed as was the Banyan Terrace.We were put in the Diamond Wing. Our room had a fantastic view of the beach and Diamond Head with a balcony. However, it smelt musty and old, the bathroom was entirely beige plastic that had seen much better days and when you turned the shower on it flooded into the bedroom. We slept there on our first night as it was 9pm, after being told at reception that the hotel was full (a third of the rooms were off limits due to rennovation).The following morning, we spoke to reception and I insisted I would not stay in the same room. We were told the hotel was full and that nothing could be done but I stood my ground. We argued that we had paid for a luxury hotel and got a room that looked like something out of Psycho to which we were told that we had already been upgraded to a room with an ocean view.I refused to leave reception until something had been sorted, at which point (after a lengthy chat with a supervisor) a room became free in the Tower Wing. It had two double beds (we were on honeymoon and American doubles are cosy to say the least) but we took the room as there was no way I could stay in the current one.The new room was much, much nicer with a partial ocean view. The bathroom was modern and clean (not really a bath to bathe in though) but compared to the other room it was like the Ritz!Although we had trouble moving our room, the staff were friendly and courteous at all times and I'm a little disappointed that we had to have the trouble with the room as the rest of the hotel could not be faulted.The poolside bar was great with superb cocktails. The pool is small but you're directly onto Waikiki Beach and shouldn't need one.Duke's bar and restaurant (part of the Outrigger next door) is a fun place to grab good food and cocktails, the menu is a little short though.The Diamond Wing that we were originally placed in is due to be refurbished in November. Once this has been completed I'm sure the hotel will be beautiful throughout and we would like to come back after this has been done when we won't have to worry about which room we'll be in!

<Author>californiamom
<Content>What hotel was this? I cannot believe that this hotel is a Westin Resort. Yes, it just changed over on June 1, but there are problems that need attention. Some of these problems can be fixed, but unfortunately others cannot. Management did generously compensate us for our difficulties, but I would not stay here again. Communication issues with personnel. We had to request things over and over to the point of exhaustion. When we received our requested items, what we wanted and what they brought were two completely different things every single time. And no, I'm not kidding. The only thing they got right was that they brought our bags to the right room. I kept asking myself where in the world was I staying? The restaurant downstairs has a mediocre breakfast buffet. I am glad we were only staying one night. I absolutely would not have been able to stay more than that. Also, we did stay in the tower. The positives are that the room was very large by hotel standards. There is also very good lighting. The location is ideal because you are in the center of all the Honolulu action. There is also the heavenly bed and heavenly shower with an interesting shower head. It had two positions on the wall: either you are very short or you are about 7' tall. Anything in between and it was kind of weird. Not sure who thought of that! The shower head was moveable, though. Oh yes, the air conditioning. The place is hot! The hallways in the tower were hot, humid and stuffy. That should have been my first indication that there is a general air conditioning problem throughout the tower. And then the room... Unfortunately if you like your room cold, our air conditioner never got below 75 degrees (and that was with leaving it on all night). I am not sure what the air conditioning system in the room was. Most hotel rooms have what I would consider central air, i.e., a thermostatic control on the wall and then a large vent on the wall just below the ceiling. This hotel has a large, silver rectangular box attached to the wall from which the air blows. The vents are on top of this silver box thing so the air actually blows up, not out. When we got to our room, the air was not on. Understand that it is pretty humid in Hawaii. Plus, a large part of the tower is completely blocked from ocean breezes because the Outrigger tower is right next door. No ceiling fan either. I like the SPG program and have been a very devoted member. I just still can't believe that this is a Westin property. I travel a lot for business and pleasure. I do consider myself a discriminating traveler. I definitely expected more. We have stayed in Honolulu several times at several other properties. We NEVER had the type of problems that we experienced at the Westin, including the air conditioning issues, so I know that this is not a general Honolulu thing. I do not think it was in Westin's best interest to convert this property. I do not like writing reviews like this, but I rely heavily on this website for recommendations and wanted to give others a heads up.

<Author>Pongdog
<Content>The First Lady Has Seen Better Days The Moana Surfrider claims to be the First Lady of Waikiki, the first hotel built on Waikiki Beach, in 1901. This hotel is sorely in need of an upgrade. We spent six nights in room 501 of the Banyan Wing. Our room overlooked the porte cochre on one side and Kalakaua Avenue 90 degrees to the right. The first thing we noticed was the street noise that reached us up on the fifth floor. Just about everything can be heard, at all hours of the day and night, as the windows were single glazed, i.e., one pane of glass, with zero insulation qualities. The loudness of the air conditioning, even on its lowest setting, helped to mask the street noise somewhat, however. The only way we were able to get a decent night's sleep was with the help of earplugs. Street performers of all types set up on Kalakaua and play until well past 11 PM. There was an obnoxious solo drummer, the obilgatory fake steel drum artist, and a female guitarist with one of those nails-on-chalkboard voices. Parking is $15 per night in a hotel garage across Kalakaua, about a 10 minute retreive, IF you can remember where you left your car. The swimming pool was chilly for May; I don't believe it was heated. At these prices you should be able to have a heated pool, one would think. The bathroom was small enough where I could stand in the middle and touch the opposite walls at the same time, in both directions. The tub was perhaps 4.5 feet long, requiring my wife to curl up to get inside. The bathroom itself did not have any means to exhaust air. You have to pay to use wired internet; a two hour block cost $4.14. The television guide is a clown act; it'll take an easy 90 seconds to load up before you can navigate to the ordinary channel function.All in all, this was a very expensive stay in a hotel that has seen better days.

I think by far it is the best place on Waikiki. That is if you get a room in the tower wing. I read others' complaints of noise on Tripadvisor before I left. The fact is the hotel is on the main drag of the biggest city in Hawaii. You're going to hear noise of the reggae players on the street and people out walking the strip. If you want quiet, you have to stay off the strip or go to a less populated island. I highly recommend this hotel if you stay in a room in the new tower. My experience would have been quite different if we would have remained in the old Banyan wing. Fortunately we got lucky and were able to switch. Whoever you are at the Sheration front desk...THANK YOU! You made our stay great!

<Author>MisrEmiri
<Content>Perfect for my dad, now 84 Our first introduction to this hotel was in 2005. After losing my mum to cancer in June 2004, I decided to take my dad on a nice vacation, in a warm climate, but staying at a historical hotel. So, this was the hotel that brought us to Hawai'i in the first place, and for that I shall always be grateful. Anyone else who has had the good fortune to visit this paradise will know exactly what I mean.We stayed here again during our last visit to Honolulu, from 13 to 21 February 2007. It seemed as though we had never left and that two years had passed between our two visits.This time around, I insisted upon staying in the Banyan Wing which is the original 1901 Moana Hotel. The Banyan Wing is undoubtedly the most beautiful part of the hotel, and if you can just block out the crowds and the din around you for a moment, you can still taste what Waikiki was once like. The corridors of the Banyan Wing are wide and quiet (deceptivly so, I regret to say). Our room was larger than our 2005 Diamond Wing room and the walls were not so paper thin that we heard the going-ons in the rooms on either side of us. However, we had a city view room (actually over the porte-cochere) and the most annoying thing was the sound of the buskers coming every evening from Kalakaua Avenue. These buskers were the same drummer and the same saxophonist (who always included a rendition of the theme from The Flintstones in his repertoire) playing the same noise each evening. Luckily, though, the buskers stopped by about 11:00pm and actually, shortly after midnight, Kalakaua Avenue quiets down all together. The room itself was quite plain; the bathroom was a decent size, but there was no closet. There is an armoire which serves as a closet and TV stand. Housekeeping was very good all around.We recognized many of the serving staff at breakfast at the Beachside Cafe all of whom we were happy to see again. The serving staff at the Beachside are always pleasant and quick to deliver anything you ask for. The views over Diamond Head and the beach are beautiful. However, if you learn only one thing from this review, please let this be it: DO NOT LEAVE YOUR TABLE UNATTENDED IF YOU ARE EATING OUTDOORS IN HAWAI'I. The birds are way too fearless and aggressive. The moment you get up from your table, they swoop down and start gorging themselves on anything and everything left on the plates. I wintessed other (novice) guests make this mistake on a few occasions, and each time this happens, the staff clear everything off the table (resulting in an often terrible waste of food). I regret, though, that I cannot be so complimentary about the food. Being a vegetarian, I have very often found dining out in Hawai'i to be challenging and sometimes frustrating. I was very often frustrated in 2005 at the food choices at this hotel, so I refused to eat anything here beyond breakfast (and I wouldn't even have done that had I not been travelling with my 84 year old dad--it was convenient for him to have breakfast here and I did so for his sake). Since this hotel is so busy, there seems to be an element of mass production when it comes to the food and the breakfast buffet was the same old same old every morning. For dinner, we went to Ciao Mein in the Hyatt Regency Waikiki across the street, or to Keoni's at the cornner of Kaiulani Avenue  Kuhio Street (which serves the most incredible tom kha soup, by the way). There is an outlet of the Honolulu Coffee Company here, serving excellent coffee and pastries. My dad patronized it so much that the staff got to know him. The hotel also has a lot of verandah space, both overlooking the ocean and Kalakaua Avenue. It is these verandahs that my dad enjoys so much and is the main reason we returned here this year. But, now for the real negatives.....The Parking!!There is no parking lot at the hotel. You have to use the parking structure behind the Sheraton Princess Kaiulani. There is no elevator in the parking structure. If you arrive back at the hotel late in the afternoon or early everning from your day's outing, you are parking on a floor high up, if not sometimes in annexes to the structure you never even knew existed!!! And this for an additional, I believe, $15 per day.Gym and business centreNeither exist in this hotel, even though there is some dead space in old lobby of the Diamond Wing that could surely accomodate a small business centre. The literature in the hotel directs you to go to the Sheraton Waikiki for both a business centre and gym, so if you want a quick visit to one or the other, you need to travel further than just the confines of your own hotel. Overall, I also found Honolulu to be even more crowded this year than the last two. I arranged a tour of Washington Place one day which is across the street from the State Capitol. I figured if I left the hotel at about 9:15am, I'd get to Washington Place in time for the 10:00am tour. No such luck; getting to the structure, getting the car down, driving along Ala Wai Boulevard, the congestive traffice on McCully Street followed by the equally congestive traffic along most of Beretania, well, I didn't make it in time!! Honolulu is roughly 17 miles long and 5 miles inland and with only three major east-west arteries (the H1, Ala Moana Boulevard and the King-Beretania combination) it seemed to take forever to move around the city. They're supposed to be starting ferry services soon between O'ahu and Kaua'i and O'ahu and Maui. If you want a quiet Hawaiian vacation, I sugges that you make Kaua'i your main base; if you want a little more activity, go to Maui. From either, do only day trips, or perhaps overnight visits to Honolulu; Explore the city, take the tours so that you see everything, but do not stay in Honolulu for more than a few nights. The sights worth seeing are, of course, Pearl Harbour, 'Iolani Palace, Diamond Head, the overlooks at Pali and Tantalus and the beaches all of which you can see on guided tours. I also suggest walking around old downtown Honolulu (in the daytime); upon learning about the history of Hawai'i during the war, films like FROM HERE TO ETERNITY take on a more familiar character.  
<Date>May 4, 2007

<Author>readyandpacked
<Content>Elegant Lady We have just returned from several days at the Moana...an Elegant Lady. Liking old hotels, we asked to stay in the Banyan Wing and were not disappointed one bit. Inside the room, the bed will be replaced with the Heavenly Bed...good, the bathroom is being modernized with only a shower....bad....and a very modern sink...horrid! The old tile floor is being replaced as well. If you are interested in historic outside and very modern inside, this is the place to go. If you are interested in historic on the outside and maintaining that dignity and ambiance throughout the hotel, forget it....or be sure you go before June when the changes will begin being made.

<Content>Great hotel if you're in Waikiki We stayed in this hotel 5 nights in Feb. 2007 and loved it. The staff was great -- everyone we encountered was extremely nice, helpful and polite. I was particularly impressed with the upkeep and maintenance of the property -- this is a large, old, highly trafficked hotel, and the part of the hotel we were in was immaculate. Dining options w/in the hotel are pricey, but there are plenty of other eating options within easy walking distance of the hotel.I would love to stay in this hotel and would highly recommend it.

Try doing some touristy shopping at Hilo Hattie's - best chocolate covered Macademia Nuts ever; Oahu Nature Tours (Manoa Waterfalls, Diamond Head Crater), XTreme Parasailing, Duke's Beachhouse Club (awesome bar!), Lulu's Bar and Restaurant (half tourists, half locals). They have free dance shows at DFS down Kalakaua Avenue, too.Note: there are a LOT of Japanese brides walking around Moana Surfrider, but aside from the picture taking, the hotel is pretty laidback.

We did have lunch a few times at the ocean bar and found it pricey. We got great food deals across the street. We used Hawaii for Dummy's to find three restaurants and were not disappointed in any of them. What with the overall cost of going first class, I would strongly recommend this book for first-timers. I compared the hotels we looked at with the book and TripAdvisor - both were quite thorough and to the point about the same places.An activity for the less physical is taking a catamaran ride - a great way to see a section of the island you are on, and we found the crew very friendly and attentive. There was one that used the beach right in front of us, and another just down the beach about 300 feet. For the more physical, there is always the trek up Diamond Head (which you can see from the beach). <Author>traveler8472
<Content>Pure heaven My husband and I stayed at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider for three nights of our honeymoon. We stayed at 6 different hotels during our honeymoon, and the Sheraton Moana Surfrider was by far our favorite. When we checked in, we were able to upgrade to an ocean-view room in the Banyan Wing. This is the older, historic part of the Moana. I had requested the Tower wing because there are lanais and it is apparently more modern, but I would not have traded our room for the world. The room was very small and did not have a lanai, so when we got in that night I was a little disappointed. However, when we woke up the next morning, my husband and I both gasped at the amazing view. It's like the ocean is in the room with you. The Moana has the most amazing location--directly on Waikiki. We thought Waikiki would be touristy, but the Moana is classic, classy, and amazingly beautiful. The lobby is all open, and you can feel the breeze of the ocean everywhere. We spent many hours just lounging on the Banyan Veranda, which is now our favorite spot in the world. The water is perfect for swimming--the best beach for relaxing and swimming that we encountered in Hawaii. We went swimming at sunset and watched the sun go down over the ocean with an awesome view of Diamond Head in the distance. When we walked around in Waikiki, we realized that we probably would not have enjoyed it nearly as much if we were not at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider. The Moana is a truly classic Hawaiian experience--it was the first luxury hotel built in the area in the early 1900s. When we were shopping on the North Shore, we found an old photo of the Moana before everything built up around it at a place that sells vintage Hawaiiana. That photo of the Moana is our favorite souvenir from the trip. We feel so fortunate that we picked the best place to stay in Waikiki. As we left the Moana, we were already planning how we would go back there for future vacations. If you love historic architecture, beachfront location, and serene beauty, you will love this hotel.

<Author>Cuteluke
<Content>Great hotel but make sure you get what you were guaranteed We just came back from a 3 night stay at this hotel. SInce it was our annivsersary, we decided to pay the extra money and booked a deluxe ocean room with a balcony. When we checked in, we were assigned to a room in the Diamond Wing on the second floor (3208). The rooms on the second floor in the Diamond Wing, have sliding glass patio doors but the balcony/lanai is at best 8 inches wide. Although we are not big people, it would have been impossible to sit on this particular laniai I phoned guest services and was told that it was a matter of interpretation. Apparently, at the Moana Surfrider, a lania means sliding glass patio doors. I almost wept. Fortunately, we were moved to another room in the wing and it had a balcony in which 2 people could sit comfortably - provided we moved the 2 chairs from the room onto the balcony. The room overlooked the Diamond Lawn and we got to watch weddings and receptions all day long. The events always ended by 10 pm and the entertainment was great. There is a Beach Club where you can reserve a chair and umbrella on the beach, but it seems one needs to know the secret handshake. Not quite sure how it works, but it's worth finding out if you're paying the big bucks to stay here. The MaiTais are some of the best on the strip and lunch at the Beachside cafe is also worth the price. The best bet for food is the Cheesecake Etc (on the main drag) The servinngs are large, the food is good, the price is right and the leftovers fit in the fridge in your room. Makes for a great snack.All in all, we would stay here again, but beware of thier definition of balcony.

<Author>brandylab
<Content>Nice Sheraton Moana Surfrider Experience We just returned from the Moana Surfrider, staying 8/31 - 9/4. We had booked a partial ocean view room and were upgraded to an ocean view room. I looked at the partial ocean view room and can say that the view was much better in the full ocean view room. We stayed in the tower on the 5th floor, just over the pool and had a lovely view of the beach and ocean with tall palm trees in front and off to the left was a great view of Diamond Head and the hotel's huge Banyan Tree. Based on prior reviews, I was bit concerned about space for the pool and the beach. I agree that the pool area is very small, really about the same size as a community pool. Even at that time of year, the lounges around the pool were crowded by about 9 am. One nice thing the hotel does is allow guests to reserve an umbrella and chairs for the next day (you have to be there by 9 am to claim the spot otherwise you will lose it). Late in the morning they bring around ice cold wash cloths for a little refreshment on the beach or at the pool. The food from the beach snack area was fresh, and was the standard hamburger/hotdog/sandwich with fries kind of thing. I found the hotel staff friendly and helpful. Shortly after arriving some single guys checked into the room next to ours. They were very loud, playing music, etc and I was concerned that the partying would continue through the night. The front desk immediately offered to either send security or move our room. I looked at the other room they offered (the partial ocean view) and decided to keep our original room. The first person I'd spoken with at the front desk called back and was concerned about the noise and offered again to send security.We had the afternoon tea on the Banyan Veranda which was lovely. We requested an ocean front table and they said they would see what they could do. Fifteen minutes before our reservation they called our room and said the table we wanted was available and we could come down anytime. We learned from our waiter that they had been holding the table for us, which we thought was very nice. The afternoon tea, although expensive, was a really nice experience - formal tea sandwiches, scones and desserts; and, the setting was lovely.The lobby of the hotel is very pretty, colonial/hawaiian style. It is not a large lobby and can be crowded, but if you go down the hall a bit, there's a much quieter area (where they often have weddings) with nice seating or rocking chairs outside to relax. The room itself, in the Tower Wing, was clean and pleasant. This was a standard Sheraton room, with comfortable beds and really nice sheets. The room did not feel small, but it did not feel large either. The bathroom had a small shower/tub combination, really only good for baths for children.The location can be good, depending on what you are looking for. It is in the heart of Waikiki, very close to the International Marketplace. Self-parking is across the street at the Sheraton Princess and can take 3 - 5 minutes to get there. Valet parking is available, but expensive ($25). Overall, I'd happily stay here again if we needed to stay in Waikiki.

<Author>AZMommy
<Content>Outstanding Service, Gorgeous Property My husband and I stayed at the Moana Surfrider for 7 nights on our honeymoon, and then came back a year and a half later with our 5 1/2 month old baby. Both times, we had the BEST overall hotel experience, and we can't wait to go back! The entire lengths of our stays, the staff was very courteous and respectful, calling us Mr. and Mrs. (last name here) any time we would call for room service, or had a question for the concierge. Even the housekeeping staff was friendly and always had a friendly greeting for us. The hotel itself is absolutely gorgeous outside, looking much like an old regal Hawaiian plantation, with huge white pillars and a circular driveway. Inside, it is decorated beautifully in what I suppose is old Hawaiian. Both times we stayed in a historic Banyan rooms. Although we were wary of this, because historic sounded like a nice way to say, old and with ratty furniture, we were pleasantly surprised. The rooms were impeccably clean, and decorated simply with authentic Hawaiian quilts on every bed. The food was great, too -- you absolutely MUST do the tea on the Veranda, and enjoy the breakfast buffet. Yes, the hotel was expensive (we paid upwards of $500 a night both times we visited), but it's worth every cent. We enjoyed it just as much when we were honeymooning, as when we were staying there with our baby. I do agree, though, that the beach is extremely crowded and they have some very strict rules at the pool. For instance, you aren't allowed to bring a little baby raft for your baby or toddler, because absolutely NO inflatables or rafts are allowed in the pool. I'm not sure why, but I suppose it's so they won't disturb other guests. But that's the only con I can think of. Anyhow, it's a great place for people of all ages, and I would wholeheartedly recommend it!

<Author>travelerof3
<Content>2nd review - parent perspective This is the second review I've written on this hotel only this time I'm a mother and my perspective is different. I hope my comments might be helpful to other parents deciding to come here. We just returned from a 5 day stay here with our 3 month old daughter and were very pleased with most of the stay. We booked a partial ocean view room and were given a most excellent room. Room 1371. (Another review stayed in 771 and sounds like they had the same layout.) I would highly recommend a room ending in 71 for a partial ocean view. The room was huge which was really nice since we had a crib, stroller, toys, etc. in it. We had 2 lanai's. One with the partial ocean view and another with a city/ mountain view. I don't know if we were given this room b/c we had a crib, but I'm not complaining. The crib that they brought us was really nice and cute. Looked comfortable. My daughter never had a problem sleeping in it. It was a little on the small side. So, if you have a squirmer like mine, watch them closely. Fortunately, the crib has bumper pads which were needed with my DD.I didn't think the hotel was as stroller/ handicap friendly as I would have liked. (Funny how you don't notice these things until you need them.) There were ramps for us to take with our stroller, but not as many. They were also deceiving. On either side of the front of the hotel, it looks like there are ramps. However on one side, there are some steps right before you get to the top of the porch. If you don't know this ahead of time, you have to head back down and around to the other side. Going to the pool/ beach area, there is a ramp to get you to the entrance of the area, but no ramp down to the area. Therefore, you have to walk all the way around to the front of the hotel to get to the pool/ beach area. No big deal. Just an FYI.We were a little disappointed with the housekeeping this time. They really didn't do a good job cleaning. We did arrange with them on the 2nd day to come at 3pm everyday which was nice. That way we could have our daughter up from her nap and be out of there when they came instead of having them bang on our door several times a day (and waking her up) wanting to know if they could come in and clean. Unfortuantely, everyday something dirty was left in the room or not cleaned. Mostly was the coffee pot, mugs, and coffee area. The one nice thing about the room which was important for me was that the room has a mini-refrigerator (no freezer section.) So, I didn't have to worry about baby's breast milk. I could pump and store as much in there as I needed.As for general hotel review (not necessairly kid related,) it was kind of noisy at night, but you're in a downtown area. What do you expect? The food was pricey. The room service menu was a little disappointing. We were in the mood for some bar type food (you know, nachos, fried cheese, burgers, etc kind of food,) but they didn't have anything like that. They had shrimp cocktail and sashimi which was good, but didn't really hit the spot. Expensive, though. They added in the tip for you and didn't give you the option of adding another one later which is nice. I always hate the way hotels add in a tip and then leave space for you to add another one. One thing that I noticed on our bill when we checked out which was a little upsetting was that they charged $1 for local calls. I looked all over to see if there was a charge for local calls, but couldn't find any info if there was. Sort of disappointing to find out afterwards. All in all a good hotel. We'll definitely keep coming back.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Afternoon Tea Is A Delight Had to post this, as there was such an unhappy review posted by someone else--sorry for that experience, but Tea on The Veranda has always been a pleasure! I was there May, 2006 and ordered the vegetarian sandwiches, as I did not care for the other choices available--no problem they were available and pleasant enough. The tea choices are excellent, and much time is given for an explantion of each variety and a chance to appreciate the fragrance of each. The service was wonderful and leisurely, with attention to refilling the teapot. You may even include champagne. Sitting on the veranda is like a wonderful trip on a time machine--you feel transported back to the days of the Matson cruise ships. I cannot imagine where else you can find that experience in Waikiki today! The large wicker chairs are very inviting, the view of the ocean is incredible, and as I said before, charming and wonderful service. I have been here many times, and regret when time does not allow an hour or so for tea here--I miss it. The sorbet is refreshing as was mentioned. The cost of the tea is not a surprise, as you have a choice of with or without the champagne, without is a bit less money. It is absolutely worth the cost, and the time spent here will stay with you forever. There is even a nice tea sample presented before you leave--a very nice touch, I think. It is the kind of experience one hopes for in tea rooms and is frequently denied. I am looking forward to the next time--have been enjoying tea here for the past 12 years. Really it's lovely.
