<Author>montya
<Content>Sensational Surfrider!!!! What a beautiful place to stay!!! We stayed at this hotel from 15-20th of June 2006. We made a last minute reservation through Starwood Preferred Guests 1 week before we left (we joined SPG 5 minutes before making the reservation, I think that it helped our stay). We requested a city view room with 2 full beds (US$260 p/n) as we were traveling with our toddler who is 21 months old. We arrived at 10.30am, were greeted with a lei and fruit juice as well as a cold face washer. Our son was given a children's lei with candy wrapped in it and a pair of kids sunglasses, instead of flowers. Our room wasn't going to be ready until 3pm, so they gave us a hospitality room (a slightly smaller than regular room with full bathroom etc. to freshen up - no beds, only sofa's). We made full use of it for about an hour, and then had our luggage stored until we got our room key later that day.When we checked in later that afternoon we were given a Tower corner room on the 7th floor- room 771 (with 2 balconies) and a decent beach/ocean view between the Tower and the Outrigger hotel next door. We were happy. Later that night, the street buskers drums started beating outside the International Marketplace which is across the street from the Surfrider. They played until about 1.30am. Our son stayed awake because of the noise, and finally fell asleep just after midnight. We were so furious. My husband went to the check-in counter the next morning at 7am and asked to be moved to a less noisy room. They moved us up one floor and towards the ocean about 4 rooms. We heard NO noise in the evenings for the next 4 nights, it was just wonderful. It was an upgrade but we didn't have to pay any more than our US$260p/n as booked.We rented a car from Thrifty for 1 day which is very conveniently located about 2 blocks away from the hotel in a parking garage. We made the reservation through DiscountHawaiiCarRental for a compact car for $28/day. They negotiated the rate with the different companies, which was a lot less than I could find anywhere else. Thrifty gave us a free upgrade to a mid-size and off we went. I will definitly use DiscountHawaiiCarRental if we return to Hawaii. They take all the pain out of looking at all the different rental car websites for quotes etc.We swam in the pool and the surf every day, and the roped off section of the beach for Surfrider patrons is a plus (that is, if you get there early enough to be so rude as to put your towels on the chairs to reserve them for hours while you are out enjoying the sights, while others could be enjoying themselves lying in the sun - selfish! You know who you are!!!). We were always there in the early morning or late afternoon, no lying around in the sun with a toddler so it didn't affect us too much, but others it did.We enjoyed our stay at the Moana Surfrider so much that we would never consider staying anywhere else if we were to return again. It is so central to everything you might need. The whole atmosphere at this hotel is relaxed, child friendly as well as honeymoonish at the same time. The views along the beach are beautiful, the weather at this time of year is superb (80's + everyday) and everyone treats you like you are an important guest.FYI, our last trip to Hawaii was in Jan/Feb 2003 and we stayed at the Hilton Hawaiian Village on the recommendation of our friends. It was good for kids (we didn't have one at that stage) as they have the birds/ fairy penguins etc. but we just felt like a number, no special treatment, boring room, and it didn't feel like it was close to much. Admittedly, it was winter and light rain most days. We had a car for the whole time we were there and spent most of the time exploring the island and driving up to the North Shore, Outlet Mall, Polynesian Cultural Centre etc, but the HHV just didn't do it for us. Also, it was more expensive than the Surfrider, even in winter.Another thing, the walk up Diamond Head is sensational. We did it with our toddler this time - my husband carried our son on his shoulders the whole way. It is quite rocky from about one third of the way up and you can't take a stroller. We got the bus one block from the Surfrider to the entrance of the Park at about 3pm and walked from there. The stairs close to the top are a killer. Once you get there, the view is superb!

<Author>FrequentFrier
<Content>City-side rooms are OK I have stayed 3 times at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider in the last year, and each time in one of the cheaper city-side rooms. They do front on to the main street in Waikiki, so traffic noise is noticeable - but this seems to subside by midnight. In the evening, visiting choirs often serenade from across the road, which is quite enjoyable. I prefer the spacious older-style rooms, and find the small bathrooms cute and functional. Being right on the beach is a big plus - and don't forget to look out for the turtles swimming with you! Meal prices are high - but there are plenty of other options within walking distance. If you have a spare hour, go on the free tour of this historic hotel. The staff have always been friendly - and the towel, guava and lei greeting is a nice way to arrive.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Grand Old Lady of Waikiki We stayed at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider February 15th to the 18th as part of a Norwegian Cruise Line package. This is the second time we have stayed at the Moana and the only thing I can say is fantastic.From the minute you check in with the warm face cloth, flowered Lai and fruit punch drink, this hotel is first class. Built in 1901 and constantly upgraded since staying there was like stepping back into history. The rooms are small and somewhat dated, however, the amenities are 5 star and the beds are extremely comfortable. You can not ask for a better location in Waikiki. The Moana is right on the beach and central to all the activity on the strip. It was so pleasant to sit on the front porch in the evening on a rocking chair and watch the activity on the street or sitting under the famous Banyan tree sipping on a cool drink and watch the surfers and beach crowd. The staff were excellent and went out of their way to accomodate any requests. I do recommend taking the organized tour of the hotel, it is very informative.The hotel restaurants are expensive, however, there are so many places to dine, it is not hard to find a reasonable place within a few minutes walking distance. Thankyou Sheraton Moana for starting our vaction off on the right foot and making us comfortable for the few days we stayed with you.For further information about the hotel and local attractions and restaurants please contact me at dcardy2@cogeco.comDave  Catherine

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Next time I'll stay in a different room or somewhere else The Moana Surfrider is a lovely old hotel with wonderful public areas but the next time I'm in Honolulu I'll definitely stay someplace else. I arrived at the hotel before my husband but the front desk refused to let me check in because they only had my husband's name on the reservation. This is a minor annoyance but I'm the one that made the reservations and they were made in both our names. Always a joy to be harassed the minute you arrive. The staff was friendly but firm in their resolve to not let me check in. We stayed in the old Banyan Court wing and had an oceanfront room without lanai. The room was extremely small which was OK but there were a few problems. When you have an oceanfront room you want to open the window coverings and see the ocean and maybe even open the windows. The problem is that the tower next door is so close to these rooms that the folks next door can peer in. Also, as other reviewers have pointed out, the windows will only open a few inches so forget the ocean breezes. Most nights you would want to keep the windows closed anyway to help block the noise from the restaurant/bar below although it does quiet down at a reasonable hour. One night there were strong winds blowing and the windows rattled in their frames all night long and created drafts through the room that caused the entry door to rattle too. She IS an OLD hotel. Another minor irritation was that the sink basin could not be closed to fill the sink with water so forget washing out the skivvies. And you'd think for these rates that you might get a free internet connection but no, they have to nickel and dime you for that too. On the plus side, the bed was very comfortable although the sheets would not stay on because they didn't fit the bed. Also, the hotel is located on a nice part of the beach with easy access to the water and friendly servers will bring you drinks and food while poolside or in the hotel's beach area. Alcohol is not allowed on the public part of the beach. (All of the waitstaff in all areas of the hotel were very friendly and accommodating.)All of these things wouldn't be such a big deal if the room rates weren't so high. I much prefer a hotel with a lanai or balcony where I can open the windows and still feel that I have some privacy, especially in the chaos that is Waikiki. Perhaps the newer, tower rooms would have been more to my liking, but they were even more expensive. We also had a pre-paid booking that made it impossible to change the room after arrival without losing money. There are better places to stay for room rates that are comparable to the Four Seasons.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Simply splendid My husband and I stayed at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider over the Thanksgiving Holiday. We were celebrating our 25th wedding anniversary.Upon our arrival, we were upgraded to a partial-ocean view room in the tower, which had a spectacular view. We left our balcony door open during the evening, and enjoyed the sound of the ocean waves throughout the night. Our room was more than adequate and thoroughly cleaned each day. The bathrooms were large, clean, and equipped very nicely. The water was always warm for showering. The beds and comforters were the best! We had no trouble getting a good night's sleep, and didn't hear any street noise as our room overlooked the ocean side. We would highly recommend staying in the tower oceanview rooms. They were large, and newly decorated. Our room was on the 9th floor. We did not spend alot of time at the hotel during the day, and chose to eat at less expensive restaurants in the area, but we did utilize the beautiful beach area, and spent several evenings having drinks underneath the Banyan tree in the courtyard...Simply splendid. The concierge was very helpful in finding us a car rental, and when we checked out on the final day, our luggage was stored and we were given a key to shower at a later time in another hotel room. In the meantime we were able to spend a few more hours on the beach before our later evening flight back to Minnesota. The hotel was just starting to decorate for the holidays, and the trees and gigantic toy soldiers were stunning. To say the least, we were extremely pleased with our stay at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider. The location is the best on the beach and close to many restaurants and shops. We would definately return to the Sheraton again if given the opportunity to go back to Hawaii.

The Moana was the very first hotel in Honolulu, built in 1908 using southern antebelleum architecure. It has, of course, been remodeled and there is a new tower next door that is also part of the original property, all in outstanding condition. The hotel offers an atrium courtyard where the focal point is a 100 plus year old Banyan tree, and of course, Waikiki beach and the sunsets. The service is excellent, and far exceeds any other resort in the area. Food at the Banyan Tree Terrace is wonderful, and on Saturday nights at 7:30 PM, the hotel offers wedding vow renewals at no charge. The live entertainment offered every evening in the courtyard is usually different original hawaiian artists, along with a hula dancer. Sipping a mai tai and listening to hawaiian music at sunset under the banyan tree at the Sheraton Moana has become my very favorite spot in Hawaii.  
<Date>Sep 19, 2005
<Rating>5	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>tequilatamm
<Content>Still the One My favourite Sheraton Property anywhere... and I've stayed at some pretty nice ones.Sure, the rooms are nothing that special, but the beautiful, grand old lobby in the Moana portion of the hotel, the rocking chairs on the old verandah, and the banyan tree area overlooking Waikiki Beach are top notch.The past few times, I have gotten great deals staying in the historic wing. I have become accustomed to this wing, as there are only a small percentage of rooms in this grand old portion of the hotel, and you actually feel as if you were in Waikiki at the turn of the century... I don't know where else you could get that.This particular trip, I was given a room on the second floor, down the Diamond Wing end of the building, and rathter than taking the elevator up one floor, I mad it habit to take the central staircase, which led me past the upstairs verandahs, and all the historic memorabilia they have on display from back in the day when this was the grand old lady of Waikiki....And then I would walk down the large, old fashioned corridor with its very Hawaiian looking carpeting (if there is such a thing) and the big old-fashioned hotel-room doors.I was fortunate enough to be in a corner room, so I had about 3 windows in my room. That combined with the new decor they have put in, including white paint, and inset mirrors behind the queen size bed, it made for a very light and airy room, with its old, very high ceilings, something you don't get in the Surfrider Tower.Unfortunately it was the wrong corner, in that it was not the corner of the building overlooking the beach, but the corner overlooking the main street of town, also with a side view of the back of the Diamond Wing!BUT.... since I got a good rate, I think I got what I paid for.As I said, the historic rooms are very nice... not all that big, but nice ambiance, and since they've put in more mirrors, it's given the illusion of being a larger room than it is, and the beautiful high ceilings.The bathrooms in the historic wing are not very large either, but put together in a way that makes it manageable.The only other thing was that, facing the street, it was a little noisy from about 10pm until about 2pm. This would probably bother most people, but since I was out partying until about midnight, by the time I went to sleep, things had calmed down on the street.The position of the hotel to the center of Waikiki Beach, the drinks at the Moana Beach Bar under the Banyan Tree, and the quick snacks out by the pool were good as ever.I will always happily come back to this hotel.

If we ever visit Waikiki again we will be staying at the Moana Surfrider. We LOVED the elegance of the hotel and location right on the beach.Enjoy your trip!

<Author>a_warm_new_year
<Content>No class -- not worth $300/night and dishonest Concierge My husband and I stayed at the Sheraton for two nights. As we walked into the hotel we were impressed with the beautiful entrance and friendly reception. Attendants comforted us with papaya juice and a cool wet towel as we checked in. In fact my mouthwash fell in the toilet as I was getting ready. The amenities were crappy.Our room was oceanfront, so we thought we'd avoided any noise from the street. Except that we were lucky enough to have The World's Most Stupidest People outside, right below the room, playing some idiotic version of Survivor. And in case we had problems listening to the competition, no worries, the hotel's MCs were equipped with microphones and speakers that boomed directly up into our room. In order to drown out the noise, we turned on the air conditioner, which would also help combat the 80F temperature of the room. Except that the fan kept clicking off every 5-10 minutes. We called the front desk, and the electrician came up promptly. The reason why the air conditioner kept cutting off was because of a sensor in the wall that kept the air conditioner off if it thought that the balcony doors were open. (The balcony was a crappy little stoop.)You'd think they would have a sign explaining this sensor business. Which brings me to another observation that there were signs plastered all over the hotel telling you what you could and could not do. No glass bottles allowed past this point. If you don't return your pool towel you will be charged $10. etc. etc. They must have some real riff-raff as guests if they need to post all these signs!The above problems would be tolerable, but not for $300/night!That evening we stopped by the concierge to find out what we needed to do to see the Pearl Harbor Memorial. The concierge informed us that there were tours at 7am, and another at 9am. Judging from the occupancy of the hotel she said we should wake up at 7am to make sure we get a spot. We were surprised by this, as we heard you could go after lunch, and so we asked if there were any alternatives, especially since we had our own car and could drive there. No there weren't, she said. It turns out she was only talking about the hotel tour. If you go to the Memorial you can stand in line, get *free* tickets for tours every 20 minutes, which consists of a movie and a boat ride to see the Arizona monument. If you go after lunch, there isn't even a line! So this concierge was very dishonest, omitting information just in the interests of making more money for the hotel. I must have missed the sign warning us of this.From the other reviews it seems your best bet is to avoid the old crappy tower (any room = 3000). I also wouldn't rely on the concierges. In general Honolulu is a waste though. I would go there just for a day trip to see the Memorial and stay in Maui the rest of the time.

The staff in the hotel and anywhere we went in Waikiki beach were the friendliest people we have ever met.Arranging the next holiday already as I can't wait to go back.

<Author>JetSet1
<Content>It couldn't be any more perfect! What a wonderful place! We were at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider from December 2 through December 6. From beginning to end all was perfect at the hotel. Our room was not small at all nor was it large; it was average size. But our view was THE BEST view in the hotel I think. We were only on the 4th floor but the view was still excellent. Imagine waking up in the morning to the sounds of the ocean waves. Then imagine sitting up in your bed, looking out the window and seeing the ocean, a half dozen or so palm trees and a beautiful view of Diamond Head--all at once while you are still sitting up in your bed!! You don't even have to walk to the balcony to see all this! All I can say is wow! If this is what you want request a room in the Tower Wing on the end that is closest to the beach--it's newer. The Banyan Wing and Historic Wing although very charming are, of course, old. I would imagine they are still well-appointed rooms but I can't vouch for that. This Hotel has a lot of history which adds a lot to the experience. The breakfast buffet was alright. They have choices of the typical American breakfast buffet or a Japanese breakfast food buffet. This hotel really caters to Japanese tourists (and there are LOTS of them there) but not overly so at the expense of their English speaking guests. The staff were great! I can't say the same for the Hyatt across the street--I think they are supposed to be bi-lingual Japanese/English but most of the Hyatt staffers I tried to talk with only spoke Japanese and very broken English. I found it difficult to find anyone there who felt comfortable speaking English with me or who even wanted to take the time to give me directions to their spa so I just went back to the Sheraton which turned out great. Our Starwood Preferred Guest membership gave us discounts for food and spa services at all the affilated Sheraton hotels there are at least 3 within a 4 block radius. I recommend the Spa at the Royal Hawaiian Sheraton affiliate (the pink hotel just a 3 minute walk away). The location of the Sheraton Moana was also excellent--next to major upscale shops like Tiffany's, Prada, Gucci, etc. They also have the open air markets just a couple blocks away where you can buy the cheaper goods and Gucci and Prada knockoffs. My only problem--reserve your pool or beach lounge chairs early because they will all be taken by 10:30 am. I also loved that the hotel has a marriage vow renewal program every Saturday night--my husband and I weren't planning to renew our vows on this trip but when we heard of the hotel's program and found out it was free we did it anyway--it was a beautiful ceremony. Oh yes--if you like piano music they have a beautiful white grand piano on the veranda facing the banyan courtyard and beach in with one of the best pianists I've heard perform. Their Hawaiian music, 3-man band is pretty good too. Our Dinner at the Veranda was great but we wanted to branch out. A French restaurant called La Mer at the Halekulani Hotel which is a short hike or short drive away is supposedly the only 5 diamond restaurant in the area--probably a good place to go for a sunset dinner if you don't mind the slightly extra expense and the semi-formal dress code. We really wanted to dine there but had to cancel our reservations to accomodate our spa appointments. Cafe Keo's is about 4 or 5 blocks away from the hotel and is a good place to go for a $3.99 egg, sausage and hash brown breakfast. They serve Thai food for lunch/dinnner. I don't imagine how anyone could be disappointed with their stay at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider (unless you want super modern rooms and get a room in the historic or Banyan wing instead) but even then the service, the location and the views are great!

<Author>calinurse
<Content>Magical!!! My sixth trip to the Waikiki area, including stays at several nearby (even next-door) hotels, but first time staying here. Now am spoiled forever! Can't imagine staying anyhere else, ifovernight at Waikiki. We were there during and right after Thanksgiving, when they first put up Christmas decorations, and it was even more stunning.The Banyan Verandah, with its big old tree lit at night, the music, the breezes, the entrance to the beach, the historical atmosphere...elegant but laid-back casual too. We had Thanksgiving dinner at Halekulani. While that's a gorgeous property, I can't imagine feeling comfortable in their outdoor bar, wearing shorts and a tee shirt. (That may be a plus for some, but not for me.) On the other hand, at Moana Surfrider, it's elegant, charming, but very relaxed--old-world spirit but informal at the same time.There are wonderful little touches that make you smile, e.g. elevators with the floor mats that change three times a day with Good Morning or Good Evening (right now they have a holiday greeting)... Christmas lights on the otuside columns...incredible architectural touches, and the way they so proudly preserve the history and spirit of this place...rocking chairs at the entry way and on the second floor above the columned entrance (our last night there, there was a parade up Kalakaua and that was a great viewing platform)...sunset from the Banyan verandah.We had a partial ocean view in the Tower Wing. The hotel was completely full and very busy, and the reception clerk seemed genuinely regretful that they were unable to upgrade us. All rooms in the Tower Wing have recently been renovated and and are bright clean and lovely, with great amenities and wondefully comfortable beds. The rooms are not large, but do have a refrigerator. Bathrooms have all sorts of goodies, including aloe vera gel, toothbrushes, toothpaste, slippers (which you can take home) and thick bathrobes (which you use, as is commonly done, only for the time you are there). Our room was very quiet, unless we opened the lanai door and heard distant sounds of traffic below on Kalakaua. Next time I'd spring for a guaranteed ocean view room. No moldy smell that some discussed, at least in this newer section of the hotel, but yes, the historical room (a fun place to visit, if you can stand the mildewed aroma) does smell like that--damp and historical, indeed.There was good, friendly and prompt service in all areas, with only a few exceptionsl Server at tea on the verandah was very talkative and helpful til after pouring the tea, then clearly forgot about us to talk to the many guests from her native land. No prob--it left us more time to relax. Then, she looked shocked (perhaps she'd forgot we wre there!) when we asked if we could have just one more tea sandwich (the answer is no). Heck, they give you as much as you like at the Ritz in London!! Also, the receptionist for the Banyan Verandah food area on the day we were there, came across as a bit of a snob as she reminded all entering guests that The Banyan Verandah tea is $25--PER PERSON. Guess they've had some shocked tea-drinkers, but I thought the way it was re-inforced was tacky.The coffee and service downstairs, off the main entryway, at the Honolulu Coffee Compay is fine, and with seats at windows that are great for people watching on the main boulevard.Only other problem is with parking. If you self-park, it is $10/day, which is normal for this area's hotels. But he lot is across the street at the Princess Kaiulani Hotel, and there are NO elevators in it. Another option is to have valet parking which is $15/day. Or, you could just rent a car for a few days--there are car rental places right across the street from the hotelThere are historical tours of the hotel three days a week. I caught the tail end of one and regretted missing it in its entirety. The man who gave it was delightful and full of intersting stories.To sum up, I can't imagine a better place to stay, if in Waikiki. There are many other details in this hotel that you'll enjoy. I loved wandering around the place, taking it all in. If you enjoy the excitement and energy of a wonderful city, the feel of velvet-textured sand and warm water on your feet (beach in front of Moana Surfrider--Outrigger Hotel area has the softest sand and best swimming in Waikiki) and an atmosphere that simply cannot be replicated, try to stay here.

<Author>TD60
<Content>A stylish, historic hotel directly on Waikiki Beach. The Hotel: The Moana Surfrider is a historic hotel that's stylishly furnished with koa antiques and traditional Hawaiian decor. My wife and I prefer the Historic Banyon View (oceanfront) rooms in the original 100 year-old building rather than the newer tower rooms. In fact, we liked the oceanfront Banyon View rooms so much that we politely declined an upgrade to a tower room on our second visit. The hotel has a gracious and professional staff, oceanfront restaurants, a stunning lobby, a beautiful courtyard with pool and other enhanced amenities. The hotel is centrally located directly on Waikiki Beach.Dining Recommendations: There are many gourmet restaurants to choose from in Hawaii (we were fortunate enough to live there for several years). On Oahu, we dined at Azul, John Dominis and Roy's to name just a few. But the best restaurant by far is Alan Wong's in Honolulu. Chef Wong's Contemporary Hawaiian Regional Cuisine includes freshly caught local seafood and scrumptious local produce. The 7-course Chef's Tasting Menu is a delightful culinary experience that you will never forget. For casual dining on Oahu, one of our favorite spots was Gordon Biersch on the waterfront at Aloha Tower Marketplace. This brewery restaurant features great beer, food and views of Honolulu harbor. The Sunday brunch buffet at the Moana Surfrider's Banyan Veranda was also very good.Conclusion: Hawaii has so much more to offer than the hustle and bustle of downtown Honolulu and Waikiki. There are many incredible natural wonders, uncrowded beaches, quaint towns and exquisite resorts throughout Hawaii. Whatever you do, don't spend more than a few days of your Hawaiian vacation in Waikiki. Plan to visit some of the other islands and see the real Hawaii, live a little!

<Content>Way to Go 'Old Lady' My wife and I spent 3 days and 2 nights at the Moana Surfrider celebrating our 30th wedding anniversary prior to going to Sheaton Maui for 6 days and 5 nights. It was our first trip to Hawaii/Honolulu and would definitely suggest you stay at the Moana if you going to Honolulu. We stayed in the Banyon section with a view of the couryard and beach. The Banyon section is part of the original hotel and reminds me of the older sections in both the Westin St. Francis-San Francisco and the Westin Essex House- New York.(both good choices on previous trips) I would suggest that you become a member of Starwood Prefered Guest (SPG) -no charge. It will give you an upgrade at check-in based upon availability. There is nothing like enjoying a cocktail in the courtyard listening to the nightly entertainment. The staff was extrememly friendly during our stay. I would suggest that you also go to the Royal Hawaiian(Sheraton) and go to the Sheraton Waikiki and ride the glass elevator to their 30th floor resturant at sunset to eat or have a cocktail and enjoy the view of Diamond Head. which are both accessable via the beach. I doubt that we will ever return to Honolulu, but for anyone who has never traveled to 50th state, spend a couple days in the Moana prior to going to Maui.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Grandam of Honolulu lives on! The Sheraton Moana Surfrider is a genteel oasis of tranquility, wedged amidst the nondescript, humdrum human concrete filing cabinets strung along Waikiki's shoreline. Saavy architects successfully blended the old with the new, the latter being a modern 21 story tower. The hotel has been recently refurbished and renovated, top to bottom, and though the tower rooms are tastefully decorated with comfortable furnishings, and tend to be larger, and offer ocean view lanai, the rooms in the older sections of the hotel are far superior in terms of ambience and refined elegance. The staff caters to your every wish without being overbearing, and genuinely strive to share the aloha spirit and assure you of a flawless and memorable stay. Online discounts are available for all room categories, but you should pay a bit more and avoid the noisy city view rooms. Remember, this historic hotel was built when Waikiki was still a calm, relaxing paradise.

<Author>lass=
<Content>Fantastic hotel! Stayed here for a week in March. Was a little apprehensive after reading some of the negative reviews on here, but needn't have worried! Had a small-medium sized (by U.S. standards) room in the 'Historic Banyan Wing' (read - original hotel building, rather than the newer, characterless towers), overlooking the central courtyard which fronts the beach. The ambience was just great - the hotel just oozes character which most other hotels in Waikiki completely lack. The room was blissfully quiet - we woke each morning to the sound of birdsong and crashing waves. I can understand how rooms facing the road would get some noise, so avoid these if you're bothered by this. The Raffles comparison quoted by soimeone earlier is not far wide of the mark! We visited a number of hotels in Waikiki during our stay, but this one is far and away the best! If anyone has any queries please feel free to e-mail me.

<Author>090909
<Content>Surfrider for Surfing, Shopping and Sun Stayed at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider the first week of April 2004. The hotel itself is an historic jewel amidst the hustle and bustle of busy Honolulu. The good: located at the premier beach location on Waikiki; beautifully restored property; the Banyan tree in the center of the hotel; great surfing on Waikiki (especially for beginners); relaxing evening music under the Banyan tree every night. The bad: very small rooms; harsh flourescent lights in the rooms; constant noise from the city side; our room was always hot and stuffy even though we had the A/C cranked at the max (65 F) - it never reached under 75 F in the room; very long wait to check in (20 minutes).I would recommend the Surfrider as long as you understand that the hotel is located smack dab in the middle of a busy city. If you want to avoid crowds or a lot of people and noise, skip Waikiki alltogether. Otherwise, come to the Surfrider to enjoy a fun visit to Honolulu that also happens to have a great beach.

<Content>Incredible Moana Surfrider - I'll be back! In October 2002, we spent our honeymoon at the Moana. When we got picked up at the airport by our transfer ride they said we were staying at the best hotel in Waikiki. We were thinking yeah right, I bet they say that to everyone. When the pulled up outside this fantastic looking hotel we couldn't believe it. It was exceptional! Total High Class. I felt I was in a movie. We had booked our honeymoon with Virgin and on arrival at the hotel we were upgraded from City View to a Historic banyan Room with views of the Banyan Tree and Partial Ocean. We never even asked. How fantastic is that! The staff were great and our room was lovely. We were barely in the room 5 minutes and someone arrived with complimentary champagne and chocolates for the honeymooners. The pool was lovely, not as big as I'd hoped but as it wasn't that busy we didn't mind. The beach is everything you have ever dreamed about for a Hawaiian beach and seeing Diamondhead in the background you really know you have arrived in paradise. If you've been there before you'll know that there is a lift in the historic building from the middle of the main lobby. We would hit the button to get the lift down each morning and peer out of the window at the sides looking at the beach while we waited. Sad but true. We had to pinch ourselves it was so unbelievably beautiful.We dined in the hotel only twice when we were there. Once for lunch and had the sunset dinner on our last night. It was lovely and the waitress was great helping us select dinner and cocktails. There are so many other great restuarants in Waikiki ... you'll be spoiled.We bought some Moana pictures from the gallery in the hotel which are proudly displayed in our home. Talking about shopping that was something else that blew me away. Most hotels have a tacky gift shop......the Moana has a Tiffanys...!! I don't think any other hotel I'll visit will ever compare to the Moana. If you are planning your holiday and thinking about the Moana, go ahead and book it. I hope you enjoy it every bit as much as we did.

The rooms are nice, just very small. Don't take a family here. That is the other thing: the walls and the celings are also very thin. We also heard the arguments of the couple next door, so if privacy is what you are looking for, you may want to opt for a newer hotel. Regardless, stop by and rock a while in the fabously rocking chairs all over the grounds. They are wonderful sunset viewing perches!!!  
<Date>Dec 6, 2003
<Rating>4	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Will only stay at the Moana Surfrider when we return This is a classic Waikiki hotel with a great deal of charm and luxury. The staff was extremely professional and courteous and bent over backwards to accommodate our requests. We originally booked a partial ocean view to save money. When we saw our room, we were not pleased. We were on the third floor looking over the roof - hardly any view of the ocean at all. This was not what we had in mind for our Waikiki vacation. We went to the front desk and requested an upgrade. Even though the hotel was fully sold out, they managed to put us into a full ocean view room for 4 nights. My recommendation - spring for the extra money - the full ocean view is well worth it!The beach is too small, but what beach isn't in Waikiki. The location, however, can't be beat. We bought air mattresses and paddled out in the ocean forever and the water never got rough (this was summer). My daughter took surfing lessons on the spot, which was very convenient.If I had one complaint, it was the quality of the fruit served for breakfast. It was supermarket quality. The pineapples tasted nothing like the delicious pineapples we had in Kauai the week before. Despite the marginal fruit, I will still give this hotel high marks.  
<Date>Nov 21, 2003
<Rating>5	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Won't be staying here again The hotel is nice but for what we paid here we got much more room and better service at other resorts. The location is good if you want to be in the middle of all the activity of Honolulu. If you want a quiet, relaxing vacation I would recommend you visit the other islands. The room was small and the bathroom even smaller. Very little room to store clothes if you are staying awhile. The room was clean and the service from the staff was so-so. I don't plan on ever vacationing in Honolulu again but if I do I would also stay somewhere else. Just not worth the price.
